The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \\\"root\\\" of the\\n2: //! borrow forwards, iterating over \\\"similar\\\" projections in lockstep until\\n3: //! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\\n4: //! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\\n5: //!\\n6: //! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\\n7: //! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\\n8: //!\\n9: //! For example, if we are comparing these:\\n10: //! ```text\\n11: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n12: //! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\\n13: //! ```\\n14: //!\\n15: //! Then our steps are:\\n16: //! ```text\\n17: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n18: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n19: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n20: //!      *x1[2].y    |  *x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n21: //!     (*x1[2].y).z | (*x1[i].y).w  -- we are disjoint and don't need to check more!\\n22: //! ```\\n23: //!\\n24: //! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\\n25: //! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\\n26: //!\\n27: //! ```text\\n28: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n29: //! ACCESS:  x1[i].y\\n30: //! ```\\n31: //!\\n32: //! Then our steps are:\\n33: //! ```text\\n34: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n35: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n36: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n37: //! ```\\n38: //!\\n39: //! -- here we run out of access - the borrow can access a part of it. If this\\n40: //! is a full deep access, then we *know* the borrow conflicts with it. However,\\n41: //! if the access is shallow, then we can proceed:\\n42: //!\\n43: //! ```text\\n44: //!       x1[2].y    | (*x1[i].y)    -- a deref! the access can't get past this, so we\\n45: //!                                     are disjoint\\n46: //! ```\\n47: //!\\n48: //! Our invariant is, that at each step of the iteration:\\n49: //!  - If we didn't run out of access to match, our borrow and access are comparable\\n50: //!    and either equal or disjoint.\\n51: //!  - If we did run out of access, the borrow can access a part of it.\\n52: \\n53: use std::cmp::max;\\n54: use std::iter;\\n55: \\n56: use rustc_hir as hir;\\n57: use rustc_middle::bug;\\n58: use to influence decisions\\n67: /// where a place might be equal or disjoint with another place, such as if `a[i] == a[j]`.\\n68: /// `PlaceConflictBias::Overlap` would bias toward assuming that `i` might equal `j` and that these\\n69: /// places overlap. `PlaceConflictBias::NoOverlap` assumes that for the purposes of the predicate\\n70: /// being run in the calling context, the conservative choice is to assume the compared indices\\n71: /// are disjoint (and therefore, do not overlap).\\n72: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq)]\\n73: pub enum PlaceConflictBias {\\n74: compared indices\n71: /// are disjoint (and therefore, do not overlap).\n72: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq)]\n73: pub enum PlaceConflictBias {\n74:     Overlap,\n75:     NoOverlap,\n76: }\n77: \n78: /// Helper function for checking if places conflict with a mutable borrow and deep access depth.\n79: /// This is used to check for places conflicting outside of the borrow checking code (such as in\n80: /// dataflow).\n81: pub fn places_conflict<'tcx>(\n82:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n83:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\n84:     borrow_place: Place<'tcx>,\n85:     access_place: Place<'tcx>,\n86:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\n87: ) -> bool {\n88:     borrow_conflicts_with_place(\n89:         tcx,\n90:         body,\n91:         borrow_place,\n92:         BorrowKind::Mut { kind: MutBorrowKind::TwoPhaseBorrow },\n93:         access_place.as_ref(),\n94:         AccessDepth::Deep,\n95:         bias,\n96:     )\n97: }\n98: \n99: /// Checks whether the `borrow_place` conflicts with the `access_place` given a borrow kind and\n100: /// access depth. The `bias` parameter is used to determine how the unknowable (comparing runtime\n101: /// array indices, for example) should be interpreted - this depends on what the caller wants in\n102: /// order to make the conservative choice and preserve soundness.\n103: #[inline]\n104: pub(super) fn borrow_conflicts_with_place<'tcx>(\n105:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n106:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\n107:     borrow_place: Place<'tcx>,\n108:     borrow_kind: BorrowKind,\n109:     access_place: PlaceRef<'tcx>,\n110:     access: AccessDepth,\n111:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\n112: ) -> bool {\n113:     let borrow_local = borrow_place.local;\n114:     let access_local = access_place.local;\n115: \n116:     if borrow_local != access_local {\n117:         // We have proven the borrow disjoint - further projections will remain disjoint.\n118:         return false;\n119:     }\n120: \n121: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/places_conflict.rs%3FL1-120"}}}

Such borrows first act as\\n5: shared borrows in a \\\"reservation\\\" phase and can later be \\\"activated\\\" into a\\n6: full mutable borrow.\\n7: \\n8: Only certain implicit mutable borrows can be two-phase, any `&mut` or `ref mut`\\n9: in the source code is never a two-phase borrow. The cases where we generate a\\n10: two-phase borrow are:\\n11: \\n12: 1. The autoref borrow when calling a method with a mutable reference receiver.\\n13: 2. A mutable reborrow in function arguments.\\n14: 3. The implicit mutable borrow in an overloaded compound assignment operator.\\n15: \\n16: \",\"endLine\":16,\"startLine\":1},{\"content\":\"86: \\n87: 1. At every location in the MIR we [check] if any two-phase borrows are\\n88:    activated at this location. If a live two phase borrow is activated at a\\n89:    location, then we check that there are no borrows that conflict with the\\n90:    two-phase borrow.\\n91: 2. At the reservation point we error if there are conflicting live *mutable*\\n92:    borrows. And lint if there are any conflicting shared borrows.\\n93: 3. Between the reservation and the activation point, the two-phase borrow acts\\n94:    as a shared borrow. We determine (in [`is_active`]) if we're at such a point\\n95:    by using the [`Dominators`] for the MIR graph.\\n96: 4. After the activation point, the two-phase borrow acts as a mutable borrow.\\n97: \\n98: [check]: https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/nightly-rustc/rustc_borrowck/struct.MirBorrowckCtxt.html#method.check_activations\\n99: [`Dominators`]: https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/nightly-rustc/rustc_data_structures/graph/dominators/struct.Dominators.html\\n100: ... [chunk truncated]\",\"endLine\":101,\"startLine\":86},{\"content\":\"67: * The point where the temporary is assigned to is called the *reservation*\\n68:   point of the two-phase borrow.\\n69: * The point where the temporary is used, which is effectively always a\\n70:   function call, is called the *activation* point.\\n71: \\n72: The activation points are found using the [`GatherBorrows`] visitor. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_017mEqeqTnjuhCa9wYkiHe98","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"59: \\n60: pub(super) fn is_active<'tcx>(\\n61:     dominators: &Dominators<BasicBlock>,\\n62:     borrow_data: &BorrowData<'tcx>,\\n63:     location: Location,\\n64: ) -> bool {\\n65:     debug!(\\\"is_active(borrow_data={:?}, location={:?})\\\", borrow_data, location);\\n66: \\n67:     let activation_location = match borrow_data.activation_location {\\n68:         // If this is not a 2-phase borrow, it is always active.\\n69:         TwoPhaseActivation::NotTwoPhase => return true,\\n70:         // And if the unique 2-phase use is not an activation, then it is *never* active.\\n71:         TwoPhaseActivation::NotActivated => return false,\\n72:         // Otherwise, we derive info from the activation point `loc`:\\n73:         TwoPhaseActivation::ActivatedAt(loc) => loc,\\n74:     };\\n75: \\n76:     // Otherwise, it is active for every location *except* in between\\n77:     // the reservation and the activation:\\n78:     //\\n79:     //       X\\n80:     //      /\\n81:     //     R      <--+ Except for this\\n82:     //    / \\\\        | diamond\\n83:     //    \\\\ /        |\\n84:     //     A  <------+\\n85:     //     |\\n86:     //     Z\\n87:     //\\n88:     // Note that we assume that:\\n89:     // - the reservation R dominates the activation A\\n90:     // - the activation A post-dominates the reservation R (ignoring unwinding edges).\\n91:     //\\n92:     // This means that there can't be an edge that leaves A and\\n93:     // comes back into that diamond unless it passes through R.\\n94:     //\\n95:     // Suboptimal: In some cases, this code walks the dominator\\n96:     // tree twice when it only has to be walked once.
